## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is a fundamental problem in population ecology. The growth rate likely depends on density-dependent feedback (P terms) and possibly time-varying environmental factors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic minus catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (compensatory density dependence)
- Seasonal/periodic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (logistic with shifting capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (general power-law density dependence)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with saturating harvest)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P → exponential/Malthusian growth regime: dP_dt ~ c*P
- Quadratic P term with negative coefficient → density-dependent self-limitation (logistic-type): dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P**2
- Product of P with logarithm of P → Gompertz-type asymmetric growth: dP_dt ~ P*log(c/P)
- Cubic polynomial in P (positive-negative-positive or negative-positive-negative signs) → Allee effect with both lower and upper population thresholds
- Fractional power of P (P**c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear growth suggesting surface-area-limited resource uptake
- Periodic functions of t multiplied by density terms → seasonally forced population dynamics
- Ratio of P to polynomial in P → compensatory or depensatory density dependence with saturation
- Difference of two power laws of P with different exponents → metabolic scaling models (anabolism vs catabolism)

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG20)

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze whether any candidate formula can match the GT expression:

**GT:** `0.1387*(-1 + P/8.038)*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(-0.5894 + P)))`

Let me first simplify the GT. Let me denote a = 0.1387, b = 8.038, d = 70.018, e = 0.5894.

**Term 1:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P
= a*P*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)
= a*P*[P/b - P²/(b*d) - 1 + P/d]
= a*[-P²/(b*d)*P + P²/b + P²/d - P]
Wait, let me expand more carefully:
= a*P*[P/b - P²/(bd) - 1 + P/d]
= a*[P²/b - P³/(bd) - P + P²/d]

**Term 2:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P` = a*P - a*P²/d

**Term 3:** `a*P/(1 + exp(-b*(P - e)))` — this is a sigmoidal term.

Combining Terms 1+2:
= a*[P²/b - P³/(bd) - P + P²/d] + a*P - a*P²/d
= a*[P²/b - P³/(bd) - P + P²/d + P - P²/d]
= a*[P²/b - P³/(bd)]
= a*P²/b*(1 - P/d)

So **GT simplifies to:** `a*P²/b*(1 - P/d) + a*P/(1 + exp(-b*(P-e)))`

This equals: `(a/b)*P² - (a/(b*d))*P³ + a*P/(1 + exp(-b*(P-e)))`

Numerically: `0.01725*P² - 0.0002464*P³ + 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(P - 0.5894)))`

The GT is a function of P only (no t dependence). So candidates with t-dependence that can't be zeroed out are eliminated.

Now I look for candidates that have:
- A cubic term in P (P³)
- A quadratic term in P (P²)
- A sigmoidal-type term involving P

The sigmoidal term `P/(1 + exp(-b*(P-e)))` can be written as `P*sigmoid(b*(P-e))`. Using the identity: `log(c*exp(Px) + 1)` relates to softplus, not exactly sigmoid times P.

**Candidate 9:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P + c3) + P*c4*c5**P + c6 + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9) + 1)`

Note: `P*c2/(P+c3)` for large P approaches c2, and `c4*c5**P` is exponential. The log term `c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9)+1)` — if c8 is very small and c9 is chosen right, this approximates a sigmoid-like function but not P*sigmoid.

**Candidate 34:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*exp(P*c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8) + 1)`

Setting c2=3 gives P³ term. Then c4*exp(P*c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8)+1). Note that `log(c7*exp(Pc8)+1) - c4*exp(Pc5)`: if c5=c8 and c4=-c6, we get c6*log(c7*exp(Pc8)+1) - c6*exp(Pc8) which doesn't give P*sigmoid.

Actually, note: d/dP [log(exp(bP)+c)] = b*exp(bP)/(exp(bP)+c), which is sigmoid-like but not multiplied by P.

None of the candidates seem to naturally produce the `P/(1+exp(...))` term. The GT has P multiplied by a sigmoid, which is structurally distinct from log-sum-exp forms or exponential forms available in the candidates.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can reproduce the `P*sigmoid(...)` structure of the GT through any parameter choice.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG20)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.13870625668024555*(-1 + P/8.038138014396704)*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*P/(1 + exp(-8.038138014396704*(-0.5894251550796137 + P)))
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.13870625668024555, a = 8.038138014396704, b = 70.01799944958296, d = 0.5894251550796137.

**Term 1:** α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
= α*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 2:** α*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 3:** α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - d)))

Combining Terms 1 and 2:
α*(1 - P/b)*P * [(-1 + P/a) + 1] = α*(1 - P/b)*P * (P/a)
= α*P²/(a*b) * (b - P) = (α/(a*b)) * P² * (b - P)
= (α/(a*b)) * (b*P² - P³)

So GT = α*P²/a - α*P³/(a*b) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

Numerically:
- α/a ≈ 0.01726
- α/(a*b) ≈ 0.000247
- The sigmoid term: α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

So GT = c_1*P² - c_2*P³ + α*P*sigmoid(a*(P-d))

The GT is a function of **P only** (no t dependence). This is critical.

**Key structural features of GT:**
1. A cubic polynomial in P (terms P² and P³)
2. A sigmoid-weighted term: P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))
3. **No dependence on t**

Now let me check each candidate. For candidates with t-dependence, I can only match if the t-dependent terms can be zeroed out.

Let me identify the basis functions needed: P³, P², and P*sigmoid(P) essentially.

The sigmoid P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) is a specific nonlinear function. It can be represented as:
- log(exp(aP) + exp(ad)) type expressions (via softplus connections)
- Or directly as a sigmoid form

Let me check which candidates could potentially match.

### Candidates with t-dependence that CAN be zeroed:
Candidates 1,2,3,4,5,7,8,10,13,14,15,16,21,22,24,25,27,28,33,41,44,50 have t terms. If t appears only in terms with free coefficients, those can be set to 0.

### Key: What functional forms can represent the sigmoid term?

The sigmoid: P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) 

Note that log(c*exp(aP) + 1) is a softplus. The sigmoid is the derivative of softplus. These are NOT the same.

P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) is NOT equivalent to log(c*exp(P*c) + 1) for any constants.

Also, c*exp(P^(1/5)) + c*(cP+1)³ + c*exp(P^(1/3)) — these are smooth functions but involve fractional powers of P, which are fundamentally different basis functions from sigmoid.

Similarly, c^P (exponential in P) is different from sigmoid.

After careful analysis, the GT requires a sigmoid function of P: P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))). 

Looking through all candidates, only candidates with `1/(1+exp(...))` or `log(c*exp(cP)+1)` type terms could potentially match.

Candidates with `log(c*exp(P*c) + 1)`: 9, 11, 20, 26, 27, 34, 35, 36, 43, 50
Candidates with `c**P`: 1,2,3,4,9,10,13,14,15,32,33,41,44
Candidates with `exp(P^(1/5))`, `(cP+1)^3`, `exp(P^(1/3))`: many others

None of these basis functions can exactly reproduce a sigmoid P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))). The softplus log(c*exp(cP)+1) is not equivalent to P*sigmoid. The exponential c^P grows without bound differently than sigmoid. The fractional power expressions are also structurally different.

After thorough analysis, **no candidate** has the correct functional form to match the GT exactly.
